<tr>
<th style="background:#E6E6FA; text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Portal:LGBT" title="Portal:LGBT">LGBT portal</a></th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Same-sex_unions" title="Template:Same-sex unions"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Same-sex_unions" title="Template talk:Same-sex unions"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Same-sex_unions&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>

</td>

</table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">Same-sex marriage</a> has been legal in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> since 3 July 2005. In 2004, the nation's newly elected <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">Socialist Party (PSOE)</a> Government, led by <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero" title="José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero">José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero</a>, began a campaign for its legalization, including the right of <a href="/wiki/LGBT_adoption" title="LGBT adoption">adoption by same-sex couples</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOD_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-SOD-1">[1]</a></sup> After much debate, a law permitting same-sex marriage was passed by the <i><a href="/wiki/Cortes_Generales" title="Cortes Generales">Cortes Generales</a></i> (Spain's <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral Parliament</a>, composed of the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Spain" title="Senate of Spain">Senate</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Deputies_(Spain)" title="Congress of Deputies (Spain)">Congress of Deputies</a>) on 30 June 2005 and published on 2 July 2005. The law took effect the next day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SPTimes_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-SPTimes-2">[2]</a></sup> making Spain the third country in the world to allow same-sex couples to marry across the entire country, after the <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_Netherlands" title="Same-sex marriage in the Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Belgium" title="Same-sex marriage in Belgium">Belgium</a>, and 17 days ahead of the right being extended across all of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Canada" title="Same-sex marriage in Canada">Canada</a>.</p>
<p>The ratification of this law was not devoid of conflict, despite support from 66% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlanOut_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-PlanOut-3">[3]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Spain" title="Roman Catholicism in Spain">Roman Catholic</a> authorities in particular were adamantly opposed, criticising what they regarded as the weakening of the meaning of marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CatholicWN_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-CatholicWN-4">[4]</a></sup> Other associations expressed concern over the possibility of lesbians and gays adopting children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20minutos_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-20minutos-5">[5]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demonstration_(people)" title="Demonstration (people)">Demonstrations</a> for and against the law drew thousands of people from all parts of Spain. After its approval, the <a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">conservative</a> <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">People's Party</a> challenged the law in the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Spain" title="Constitutional Court of Spain">Constitutional Court</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Approximately 4,500 same-sex couples married in Spain during the first year of the law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Shortly after the law was passed, questions arose about the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legal_status" title="Legal status">legal status</a> of marriage to non-Spaniards whose country did not permit same-sex marriage. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Court_ruling" title="Court ruling">ruling</a> from the Justice Ministry stated that the country's same-sex marriage law allows a Spanish citizen to marry a non-Spaniard regardless of whether that person's <a href="/wiki/Nationality" title="Nationality">homeland</a> recognizes the partnership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-advocate_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-advocate-8">[8]</a></sup> At least one partner must be a Spanish citizen in order to marry, although two non-Spaniards may marry if they both have legal <a href="/wiki/Permanent_residency" title="Permanent residency">residence</a> in Spain.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_general_election,_2011" title="Spanish general election, 2011">November 2011 general election</a> delivered a landslide victory to the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">People's Party</a>, whose leader <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">Mariano Rajoy</a> said that he opposed same-sex marriage, but any decision about repealing the law could be made only after the ruling of the Constitutional Court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Backlash_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Backlash-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Factbook_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Huffpost_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Huffpost-11">[11]</a></sup> On 6 November 2012, the law was upheld by the Court with 8 support votes and 3 against.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Minister of Justice <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Ruiz-Gallard%C3%B3n" title="Alberto Ruiz-Gallardón">Alberto Ruiz-Gallardón</a> announced that the Government will abide the ruling and the law will not be repealed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Same-sex_marriage_in_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Same-sex_marriage_map_Europe_detailed.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="680" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Same-sex_marriage_map_Europe_detailed.svg/200px-Same-sex_marriage_map_Europe_detailed.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Same-sex_marriage_map_Europe_detailed.svg/300px-Same-sex_marriage_map_Europe_detailed.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Same-sex_marriage_map_Europe_detailed.svg/400px-Same-sex_marriage_map_Europe_detailed.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Same-sex_marriage_map_Europe_detailed.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<b>Laws regarding same-sex partnerships in Europe</b>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000445; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Marriage</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00ffde; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Foreign marriages recognized</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0066FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Other type of partnership</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #AACCFF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Unregistered cohabitation</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #cccccc; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Unrecognized</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #D40000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Constitution limits marriage to opposite-sex couples</div>
<hr/>
<small>Includes laws that have not yet gone into effect.</small>
<div align="right">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Same-sex_marriage_map_Europe" title="Template:Same-sex marriage map Europe"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Same-sex_marriage_map_Europe" title="Template talk:Same-sex marriage map Europe"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Same-sex_marriage_map_Europe&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the 1990s and early 2000s, several city councils and <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous communities</a> had opened registers for <a href="/wiki/Civil_union" title="Civil union">civil unions</a> that allowed benefits for unmarried couples of any sex, although the effect was mainly symbolic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-equality_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-equality-18">[18]</a></sup> Registries were created in 16 out of 17 of Spain's autonomous communities; <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> (1998), <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragon</a> (1999), <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">Navarre</a> (2000), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castile-La_Mancha" title="Castile-La Mancha">Castile-La Mancha</a> (2000), <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencia</a> (2001), <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> (2001), <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Madrid" title="Community of Madrid">Madrid</a> (2001), <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a> (2002), <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a> (2002), <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile and León</a> (2002), <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremadura</a> (2003), <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a> (2003), <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> (2003), <a href="/wiki/Cantabria" title="Cantabria">Cantabria</a> (2005), <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> (2008) and <a href="/wiki/La_Rioja_(Spain)" title="La Rioja (Spain)">La Rioja</a> (2010), and in both autonomous cities; <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> (1998) and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> (2008)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Spanish law already allowed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single_(relationship)" title="Single (relationship)">single</a> people to adopt children; thus, a same-sex couple could undertake a <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> adoption, but the partner who was not the legal parent had no rights if the relationship ended or the legal parent died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-equality_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-equality-18">[18]</a></sup> Same-sex marriages were not legal in the autonomous communities, because the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution</a> gives the State sole power to legislate marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-equality_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-equality-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pedro_Zerolo_2013.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2425" data-file-width="1689" height="287" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Pedro_Zerolo_2013.png/200px-Pedro_Zerolo_2013.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Pedro_Zerolo_2013.png/300px-Pedro_Zerolo_2013.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Pedro_Zerolo_2013.png/400px-Pedro_Zerolo_2013.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pedro_Zerolo_2013.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Politician <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Zerolo" title="Pedro Zerolo">Pedro Zerolo</a> was one of the most important LGBT activists in the history of Spain and one of the biggest promoters of extending the right to marriage and adoption to homosexual couples in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">Socialist Party (PSOE)</a> manifesto for the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_general_election,_2004" title="Spanish general election, 2004">2004 general election</a> included the pledge of amending the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_Code" title="Civil Code">Civil Code</a> to legalize same-sex marriage, granting it the same status as heterosexual marriage in order to "ensure full social and legal equality for lesbians and gays".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> After the socialists' victory in the election, the new <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero" title="José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero">José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero</a>, promised at his inauguration address to bring this change forward: "The moment has finally arrived to end once and for all the intolerable discrimination which many Spaniards suffer because of their sexual preferences. (...) As a result, we will modify the Civil Code to recognize their equal right to marriage with the resulting effects over inheritance, labor rights and social security protection".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOD_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-SOD-1">[1]</a></sup> On 30 June 2004, then Minister of Justice <a href="/wiki/Juan_Fernando_L%C3%B3pez_Aguilar" title="Juan Fernando López Aguilar">Juan Fernando López Aguilar</a> announced that the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Deputies_(Spain)" title="Congress of Deputies (Spain)">Congress of Deputies</a> had provisionally approved a government plan for legislation to extend the right of marriage to same-sex couples. López Aguilar also announced two propositions, introduced by the regional <a href="/wiki/Convergence_and_Union" title="Convergence and Union">Convergence and Union</a> party of <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>: one introduced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legal_status" title="Legal status">legal status</a> for both opposite- and same-sex <a href="/wiki/Common-law_marriage" title="Common-law marriage">common-law unions</a> (<i>parejas de hecho</i>, "de facto unions"), while the other permitted <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> people to legally <a href="/wiki/Name_change" title="Name change">change their name</a> and sex designation without the requirement of <a href="/wiki/Sex_reassignment_surgery" title="Sex reassignment surgery">surgery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Advocate_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Advocate-30">[30]</a></sup> The bill regarding same-sex marriage was approved by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Spain" title="Cabinet of Spain">Cabinet</a> on 1 October 2004, submitted to Parliament on 31 December,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> and passed by the Congress of Deputies on 21 April 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> However, it was rejected on 22 June 2005 by the Senate, where the opposition <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">People's Party</a> held a plurality of the seats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The bill was returned to the lower house, which holds the power to override the Senate, and final approval was given to the bill on 30 June 2005 with 187 "yes" votes, 147 "no" votes, and 4 abstentions.</p>
<p>With the final approval, and enactment of the bill on 2 July 2005, Spain became the third country in the world to formally legalize same-sex marriages nationwide, after the <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_Netherlands" title="Same-sex marriage in the Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Belgium" title="Same-sex marriage in Belgium">Belgium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first same-sex wedding took place eight days after the bill became law, and was celebrated in the council chamber in the <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> suburb of <a href="/wiki/Tres_Cantos" title="Tres Cantos">Tres Cantos</a> by Carlos Baturín and Emilio Menéndez.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The first same-sex marriage between women took place in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> eleven days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>In spite of these steps toward <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equal_treatment" title="Equal treatment">equal treatment</a>, a legal flaw remained: if children were born within a <a href="/wiki/Lesbian" title="Lesbian">lesbian</a> marriage, the non-biological mother was not legally regarded as a parent; she still had to undergo the lengthy financial process of adoption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> This right was granted to heterosexual couples (married or not), where a stepfather could declare his wife's children to be his without further process. On 7 November 2006, the Spanish Parliament amended the law on <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_technology" title="Reproductive technology">assisted reproduction</a>, allowing the non-biological mother to be regarded as a parent alongside her female spouse who is the birth-mother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ratification_of_Law_13.2F2005">Ratification of Law 13/2005</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Same-sex_marriage_in_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Ratification of Law 13/2005">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The projected bill announced on 30 June 2004 by the Minister of Justice was studied by the <a href="/wiki/General_Council_of_the_Judiciary" title="General Council of the Judiciary">General Council of the Judiciary</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Although the General Council admitted that the existing discrimination against homosexuals could not be condoned, it was quite critical about extending marriage toward same-sex couples (including collateral adoption). It argued that the extension was not demanded by the Constitution, and that ending discrimination could be achieved through other legal means, such as the extension of civil unions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite this negative report, the Government presented the bill to Congress on 1 October 2004. With the exception of the People's Party and members of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Union_of_Catalonia" title="Democratic Union of Catalonia">Democratic Union of Catalonia</a>, the different parliamentary parties favoured the reform. On 21 April 2005, Congress approved the bill, with 183 "yes" (including a member of the People's Party) and 136 "no" votes and 6 abstentions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The bill to allow same-sex marriage in Spain was short: it added a new paragraph to Article 44 of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_Code" title="Civil Code">Civil Code</a>, saying that <i>Matrimony shall have the same requisites and effects regardless of whether the persons involved are of the same or different sex</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>

</td>

<td><span style="background-color:#DD0505; color:; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">    </span> <a href="/wiki/Nafarroa_Bai" title="Nafarroa Bai">Yes to Navarre (NaBai)</a></td>
<td style="background-color:#CCFFCC;">
<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border: none; padding: 0;">
<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background: transparent; text-align: left;">1</div>
<ul class="NavContent" style="list-style: none none; margin-left: 0; text-align: left; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;">
<li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Uxue_Barkos" title="Uxue Barkos">María Uxue Barkos Berruezo</a></li>
</ul>

<td style="text-align:center;">Total</td>
<td class="table-yes" style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;"><b>183</b></td>

<td style="text-align:center;"><b>25</b></td>

<p>In accordance with constitutional provisions, the text approved by the Congress was then submitted to the Senate for final approval, change or <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">veto</a>. On 21 June 2005, experts were called to the Senate to debate the issue. The expert's opinions were diverse; some stated that <a href="/wiki/LGBT_adoption" title="LGBT adoption">same-sex adoption</a> had no effect on a child's <a href="/wiki/Child_development" title="Child development">development</a>, except for perhaps a higher tolerance towards homosexuality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> However, psychiatrist Aquilino Polaino, called by the People's Party as an expert, called homosexuality a <a href="/wiki/Pathology" title="Pathology">pathology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emotional_and_behavioral_disorders" title="Emotional and behavioral disorders">emotive disorder</a>. Among other assertions that generated debate, he claimed that "many homosexuals have rape abuse antecedents since childhood" and that homosexuals generally come from families with "hostile, <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">alcoholic</a> and distant" fathers, and mothers who were "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Over_protective" title="Over protective">over protective</a>" toward boys and "cold" toward girls. Prominent People's Party members later rejected Polaino's assertions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em">
<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Same-sex marriage in Spain</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="external text" href="https://www.boe.es/buscar/doc.php?id=BOE-A-2005-11364" rel="nofollow"><i>Ley 13/2005 por la que se modifica el Código Civil en materia de derecho a contraer matrimonio.</i></a> (Law 13/2005 that amends the Civil Code regarding the right to contract marriage)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Date signed</th>
<td>1 July 2005</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Introduced by</th>
<td><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero" title="José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero">José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">PSOE</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The Senate vetoed the text submitted by the Congress. The veto was proposed by the People's Party, which held the majority of the seats, and by the Democratic Union of Catalonia, and was approved by 131 "yes" and 119 "no" votes and 2 abstentions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> As a result, the text was sent back to the Congress. On 30 June 2005, it was approved by Congress, which, in accordance with the constitutional provisions, overrode the Senate veto. This was achieved with 187 "yes" votes (including a member of the People's Party, <a href="/wiki/Celia_Villalobos" title="Celia Villalobos">Celia Villalobos</a>), 147 "no" votes, and four abstentions. The veto override implied its approval as law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SPTimes_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-SPTimes-2">[2]</a></sup> The vote was held after Zapatero unexpectedly took the floor of Parliament to speak in its support, saying <i>We are expanding the opportunities for happiness of our neighbors, our colleagues, our friends and our relatives. At the same time, we are building a more decent society.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WashingP_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-WashingP-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">Mariano Rajoy</a>, the leader of the opposition People's Party, was denied the opportunity to address Parliament after Zapatero's appearance, and accused Zapatero of dividing Spanish society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WashingP_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-WashingP-48">[48]</a></sup></p>

<td><span style="background-color:#DD0505; color:; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">    </span> <a href="/wiki/Nafarroa_Bai" title="Nafarroa Bai">Yes to Navarre (NaBai)</a></td>
<td style="background-color:#CCFFCC;">
<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border: none; padding: 0;">
<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background: transparent; text-align: left;">1</div>

<td style="text-align:center;">Total</td>
<td class="table-yes" style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;"><b>187</b></td>
<td style="text-align:center;"><b>147</b></td>
<td style="text-align:center;"><b>4</b></td>
<td style="text-align:center;"><b>12</b></td>

</table>
<p>When the media asked <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">King</a> <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_I_of_Spain" title="Juan Carlos I of Spain">Juan Carlos</a> if he would sign the bill that was being debated in the <i>Cortes Generales</i>, he answered that he was the King of Spain, not of <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Belgium" title="Monarchy of Belgium">Belgium</a> – a reference to King <a href="/wiki/Baudouin_of_Belgium" title="Baudouin of Belgium">Baudouin of Belgium</a>, who refused to sign the Belgian law legalising <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">abortion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> For the King to withhold his <a href="/wiki/Royal_assent" title="Royal assent">royal assent</a>, it would effect a veto of the legislation. However, the King gave his royal assent to Law 13/2005 on 1 July 2005, and the law was <a href="/wiki/Gazette" title="Gazette">gazetted</a> in the <i><a href="/wiki/Bolet%C3%ADn_Oficial_del_Estado" title="Boletín Oficial del Estado">Boletín Oficial del Estado</a></i> on 2 July, and came into effect on 3 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The King received criticism by <a href="/wiki/Carlism" title="Carlism">Carlist</a> and other far right conservatives for signing the legislation.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Same-sex_marriage_in_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gay_March_celebrating_2005_Pride_Day_and_Same-Sex_Marriage_Law_in_Spain.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="280" data-file-width="247" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Gay_March_celebrating_2005_Pride_Day_and_Same-Sex_Marriage_Law_in_Spain.jpg/220px-Gay_March_celebrating_2005_Pride_Day_and_Same-Sex_Marriage_Law_in_Spain.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7c/Gay_March_celebrating_2005_Pride_Day_and_Same-Sex_Marriage_Law_in_Spain.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gay_March_celebrating_2005_Pride_Day_and_Same-Sex_Marriage_Law_in_Spain.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gay march celebrating Pride Day and legalization of same-sex marriage</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The bill's passage was met with concern by Catholic authorities, including <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> — who warned of a weakening of <a href="/wiki/Family_values" title="Family values">family values</a> — and his successor <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCnews_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCnews-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_L%C3%B3pez_Trujillo" title="Alfonso López Trujillo">Cardinal López Trujillo</a>, president of the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Council_for_the_Family" title="Pontifical Council for the Family">Pontifical Council for the Family</a>, said the Church was making an urgent call for <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_thought" title="Freedom of thought">freedom of conscience</a> for Catholics and appealing to them to resist the law. He said every profession linked with implementing same-sex marriages should oppose it, even if it meant losing their jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCnews_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBCnews-52">[52]</a></sup> Gay rights supporters argued that while the Catholic Church also formally opposed opposite-sex, non-religious marriage, its opposition was not as vocal; for example, the Church did not object to the marriage of <a href="/wiki/Felipe_VI_of_Spain" title="Felipe VI of Spain">Prince Felipe</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Letizia_Ortiz" title="Letizia Ortiz">Letizia Ortiz</a>, who had divorced from a previous civil marriage. The church was unable to gather enough support to derail the bill, even though 80% of Spaniards identify as members of the Catholic Faith. <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">Sociologists</a> believe this may be due to the significant increase of <a href="/wiki/Cultural_liberalism" title="Cultural liberalism">liberalism</a> in the realm of individual rights in recent years, where the Church traditionally had most influence, especially on family issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> A poll showed that three quarters of Spaniards believe the church hierarchy is out of touch with social reality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> A complementary explanation might be that the Church's influence on Spaniards declined after the death in 1975 of the <a href="/wiki/Dictator" title="Dictator">dictator</a> General <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a>, whose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spain_under_Franco" title="Spain under Franco">regime</a> was closely linked to the Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prime Minister Zapatero responded to Church criticism by saying:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>There is no damage to marriage or to the family in allowing two people of the same sex to get married. Rather, these citizens now have the ability to organize<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> their lives according to marital and familial norms and demands. There is no threat to the institution of marriage, but precisely the opposite: this law recognizes and values marriage.<br/>
<br/>
Aware that some people and institutions profoundly disagree with this legal change, I wish to say that like other reforms to the marriage code that preceded this one, this law will not generate bad results, that its only consequence will be to avoid senseless suffering of human beings. A society that avoids senseless suffering of its citizens is a better society.<br/>
<br/>
In any case, I wish to express my deep respect to those people and institutions, and I also want to ask for the same respect for all of those who approve of this law. To the homosexuals that have personally tolerated the abuse and insults for many years, I ask that you add to the courage you have demonstrated in your struggle for civil rights, an example of generosity and joy with respect to all the beliefs.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— Spanish Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero" title="José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero">José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:141px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Family_Forum_march_supporter_(not_blurred).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="172" data-file-width="139" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f8/Family_Forum_march_supporter_%28not_blurred%29.jpg" width="139"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Family_Forum_march_supporter_(not_blurred).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Same-sex marriage opposer showing banner 'Marriage = Man and Woman'</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 19 June 2005, there was a public protest against the law. Protesters — led by People's Party members, <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_Roman_Catholic_dioceses_of_Spain" title="List of the Roman Catholic dioceses of Spain">Spanish bishops</a> and the Spanish Family Forum (<i>Foro Español de la Familia</i>) — said they had rallied 1.5 million people against what they considered an attack on the traditional family and Spanish values; the Government's Delegation in Madrid counted 166,000 at the same event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Two weeks after this protest, coinciding with <a href="/wiki/Gay_pride" title="Gay pride">Gay Pride</a> Day, FELGT (<i>Federación Estatal de Lesbianas, Gays, Transexuales y Bisexuales</i> — the Spanish Lesbian, Gay, and Transgender Organization) estimated two million people marched in favour of the new law; police sources counted 97,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Both marches took place in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, at the time governed by the conservative People's Party.</p>
<p>Spanish bishops also claimed that the Government, by extending the right of marriage to same-sex couples, weakened the meaning of marriage, which they defined as an involving a heterosexual couple.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CatholicWN_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-CatholicWN-4">[4]</a></sup> The Spanish Family Forum expressed concern over the possibility of same-sex couples adopting and raising children, and argued that <a href="/wiki/Adoption" title="Adoption">adoption</a> is not a right for the parents, but for the adopted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20minutos_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-20minutos-5">[5]</a></sup> Gay associations replied that de facto adoption by same-sex couples had existed for a long time in Spain, since many couples were rearing minors adopted by one of the partners. Adoption by same-sex couples was already legal in <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">Navarre</a> (2000), the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a> (2003), <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragon</a> (2004), <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> (2005) and <a href="/wiki/Cantabria" title="Cantabria">Cantabria</a> (2005) before the same-sex marriage law legalized these adoptions nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Furthermore, in <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a> (2002), <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a> (2002) and <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremadura</a> (2003), same-sex couples could jointly begin procedures to temporarily or permanently take children in care. These associations also argued that there was no scientific basis for the claim that the parents' <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexual orientation</a> would cause developmental problems for their adopted children. This view is officially supported by the Spanish School of <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">Psychology</a>, which also states that homosexuality is not a pathology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a 2008 biography, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Sofia_of_Spain" title="Queen Sofia of Spain">Queen Sofia of Spain</a> revealed that she preferred the term "civil union" to "marriage" for committed same-sex relationships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_Sofia_Unamused_by_a_Book_Quoting_Her_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_Sofia_Unamused_by_a_Book_Quoting_Her-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_of_Spain.27s_Gay_Marriage_Comment_Ignites_Controversy_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_of_Spain.27s_Gay_Marriage_Comment_Ignites_Controversy-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen.27s_outburst_sparks_debate_about_the_monarchy_in_Spain_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Queen.27s_outburst_sparks_debate_about_the_monarchy_in_Spain-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spain.27s_queen_criticized_for_anti-gay_comments_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spain.27s_queen_criticized_for_anti-gay_comments-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spanish_Queen_alone_in_anti-gay_comments_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spanish_Queen_alone_in_anti-gay_comments-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gay_Anger_Over_Spanish_Queen_Book_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gay_Anger_Over_Spanish_Queen_Book-69">[69]</a></sup> This and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alleged" title="Alleged">alleged</a> comments by the Queen opened the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">Spanish monarchy</a> to rare criticism in 2008, with the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Zarzuela" title="Palace of Zarzuela">Zarzuela palace</a> issuing an apology on behalf of the Queen for the "inexact" quotes attributed to her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen.27s_outburst_sparks_debate_about_the_monarchy_in_Spain_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Queen.27s_outburst_sparks_debate_about_the_monarchy_in_Spain-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_draws_ire_over_gay_marriage_comment_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_draws_ire_over_gay_marriage_comment-70">[70]</a></sup> Antonio Poveda, president of FELGT, said his organization accepted the Queen's apology, but added that there remains ill feelings by the <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Spain" title="LGBT rights in Spain">gay community</a> towards the Queen over the comments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_Sofia_Unamused_by_a_Book_Quoting_Her_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_Sofia_Unamused_by_a_Book_Quoting_Her-64">[64]</a></sup> King Juan Carlos, known to be far more liberal than his wife, was reportedly incensed by the biography, with reporters stating the King will fire palace officials who allegedly approved official royal endorsement of the book.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_Sofia_Unamused_by_a_Book_Quoting_Her_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_Sofia_Unamused_by_a_Book_Quoting_Her-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 2011 General Election, People's Party leader and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_minister_of_Spain" title="Prime minister of Spain">Prime Minister of Spain</a> <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">Mariano Rajoy</a> stated he also prefers the term "civil union" to marriage for same-sex couples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Backlash_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Backlash-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Factbook_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Huffpost_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Huffpost-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_court_challenges">Opposition court challenges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Same-sex_marriage_in_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Opposition court challenges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 21 July 2005, a judge from the city of <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9nia" title="Dénia">Dénia</a> refused to issue a marriage license to a lesbian couple. The judge also filed a constitutional challenge against the same-sex marriage law before the Constitutional Court based on Article 32 of the Constitution that contains the phrase "Men and women have the right to contract marriage with full juridical equality."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In August 2005, a judge from <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a> refused licenses to three same-sex couples and mounted another constitutional challenge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In December 2005, the Constitutional Court rejected both challenges owing to both judges' lack of <a href="/wiki/Standing_(law)" title="Standing (law)">standing</a> to file them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> On 30 September 2005, the opposition People's Party decided to initiate a separate constitutional challenge, causing division within the party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The outcome was published on 6 November 2012, seven years after the challenge was presented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The Court decided to uphold the same-sex marriage law with 8 support votes and 3 against.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 February 2007, the Spanish Family Forum presented an initiative signed by 1.5 million people to legislate marriage as the union of a man and a woman only (thus effectively prohibiting same-sex marriage). The initiative was rejected by the Spanish Congress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> On 30 May 2007, the aforementioned judge of Dénia was condemned by the Disciplinary Committee of the General Council of Judiciary Power (<i>Comisión Disciplinaria del Consejo General del Poder Judicial -CGPJ-</i>) to pay 305 euros for refusing to marry a gay couple and was also strictly warned against doing it again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denia_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Denia-78">[78]</a></sup> She attributes this action to the "propagandistic machinery" of the Government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denia_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Denia-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Residency_issues">Residency issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Same-sex_marriage_in_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Residency issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World_marriage-equality_laws.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="863" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/World_marriage-equality_laws.svg/330px-World_marriage-equality_laws.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/World_marriage-equality_laws.svg/495px-World_marriage-equality_laws.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/World_marriage-equality_laws.svg/660px-World_marriage-equality_laws.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World_marriage-equality_laws.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #002255; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Marriage open to same-sex couples</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #008080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Recognized or performed in limited circumstances</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #DECD87; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Government has announced intention to legalize</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #CCCCCC; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Same-sex marriage not legally recognized</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Shortly after the law was passed, questions arose about the legal status of marriage to non-Spaniards after a Spaniard and an Indian national living in <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> were denied a marriage license on the grounds that India <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality_in_India" title="Homosexuality in India">did not permit</a> same-sex marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> However, on 22 July, another judge in Catalonia married a Spanish woman and her <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentinian</a> national partner (the <a href="/wiki/First_same-sex_marriage_in_Spain" title="First same-sex marriage in Spain">first same-sex marriage between women in Spain</a>). This judge disagreed with his colleague's decision and gave preference to the right of marriage over Argentinian law at the time not allowing same-sex marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 July, the <i>Junta de Fiscales de Sala</i> – a body within the Public Prosecutor's Corp that advises the Minister of Justice's office – issued an opinion that <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> Spaniards can marry foreigners from countries that do not permit same-sex marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> This marriage would be valid according to Spanish law, but did not imply automatic validity according to the foreigner's national law. A ruling published in the Official State Bulletin stated:</p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;"><i>a marriage between a Spaniard and a foreigner, or between foreigners of the same sex resident in Spain, shall be valid as a result of applying Spanish material law, even if the foreigner's national legislation does not allow or recognize the validity of such marriages.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-advocate_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-advocate-8">[8]</a></sup></td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>According to the instructions from the Ministry of Justice (<i>Dirección General de Registros y Notariado</i>), <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Spain" title="Foreign relations of Spain">Spanish Consulates</a> abroad may carry out the preliminary paperwork for a same-sex marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> At least one of the marrying partners must be a Spanish citizen, residing in the Consular demarcation. However, the marriage itself can only take place at the <a href="/wiki/Consul_(representative)" title="Consul (representative)">Consulate</a> if local laws recognize same-sex marriages. In all other cases, the partners must marry in Spanish territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Two non-resident foreigners cannot marry in Spain, as at least one of the partners must be a Spanish resident, although they both may be non-Spanish citizens.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_statistics">Marriage statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Same-sex_marriage_in_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Marriage statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matrimonios_homosexuales_en_Espa%C3%B1a_2008.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="643" data-file-width="700" height="276" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Matrimonios_homosexuales_en_Espa%C3%B1a_2008.svg/300px-Matrimonios_homosexuales_en_Espa%C3%B1a_2008.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Matrimonios_homosexuales_en_Espa%C3%B1a_2008.svg/450px-Matrimonios_homosexuales_en_Espa%C3%B1a_2008.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Matrimonios_homosexuales_en_Espa%C3%B1a_2008.svg/600px-Matrimonios_homosexuales_en_Espa%C3%B1a_2008.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matrimonios_homosexuales_en_Espa%C3%B1a_2008.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marriage_rates" title="Marriage rates">Marriage rates</a> of same-sex marriages in Spain in 2008
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #faa6a6; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> 0.127–0.06</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #dcb9ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> 0.06–0.04</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b3defd; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> 0.04–0.02</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #326599; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> 0.02–0.013</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the Spanish National Statistics Institute (INE), 37,441 same-sex marriages took place up to the end of 2015: 1,275 in 2005,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> 4,574 in 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> 3,250 in 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> 3,549 in 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> 3,412 in 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> 3,583 in 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> 3,880 in 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> 3,834 in 2012, <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> 3,071 in 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> 3,275 in 2014<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> and 3,738 in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistics2015_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Statistics2015-94">[94]</a></sup></p>

<p>Most same-sex marriages in 2011 took place in: <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> with 886 weddings (3.33% of all marriages in the community for that year), <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> with 729 marriages (2.91%), <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a> with 484 (1.71%), <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencia</a> with 436 (2.58%) and the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> with 203 (3.60%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 July 2015, the Spanish National Statistics Institute revealed that 31,640 same-sex couples had married since the start of July 2005 (when same-sex marriage became legal in Spain) to the end of December 2014. This accounted for 1.72% of all marriages in Spain in that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> In 2015, most same-sex marriages were celebrated in Catalonia (799), Madrid (726), Andalusia (575), Valencia (471) and the Canary Islands (265).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statistics2015_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-Statistics2015-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_weddings">Notable weddings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Same-sex_marriage_in_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Notable weddings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since its legalization in 2005, couples from a cross section of Spanish society have entered into same-sex marriages. Within the first year the law received royal assent, an influential <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">socialist</a> leader and <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> city councilor <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Zerolo" title="Pedro Zerolo">Pedro Zerolo</a> married Jesús Santos in January, and popular television presenter <a href="/wiki/Jes%C3%BAs_V%C3%A1zquez_(television_presenter)" title="Jesús Vázquez (television presenter)">Jesús Vázquez</a> married Roberto Cortés in March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zerolo.27s_wedding_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zerolo.27s_wedding-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jes.C3.BAs_V.C3.A1zquez.27s_wedding_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jes.C3.BAs_V.C3.A1zquez.27s_wedding-98">[98]</a></sup> In October 2005, Spain's prominent <a href="/wiki/Anti-terrorism_legislation" title="Anti-terrorism legislation">anti-terrorism judge</a> Fernando Grande-Marlaska married his fiancé Gorka Gómez.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fernando_Grande-Marlaska.27s_wedding_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fernando_Grande-Marlaska.27s_wedding-99">[99]</a></sup> In August 2006, <a href="/wiki/Ourense" title="Ourense">Ourense</a> city councilor and member of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">People's Party</a> Pepe Araujo, whose party originally opposed the law, married his fiancé Nino Crespo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conservative_PP_member_weds_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Conservative_PP_member_weds-100">[100]</a></sup> In September 2006, Alberto Linero Marchena and Alberto Sánchez Fernández, both army soldiers assigned to the <a href="/wiki/Mor%C3%B3n_Air_Base" title="Morón Air Base">Morón Air Base</a> near <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, became Spain's first <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armed_Forces" title="Spanish Armed Forces">military personnel</a> to marry under the new law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spanish_army_soldiers_wed_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spanish_army_soldiers_wed-101">[101]</a></sup> In August 2008, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Do%C3%B1a" title="Doña">Doña</a> <a href="/wiki/Luisa_Isabel_%C3%81lvarez_de_Toledo,_21st_Duchess_of_Medina_Sidonia" title="Luisa Isabel Álvarez de Toledo, 21st Duchess of Medina Sidonia">Luisa Isabel Álvarez de Toledo, 21st Duchess of Medina Sidonia</a> and three-time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grandee_of_Spain" title="Grandee of Spain">Grandee of Spain</a> (branded the <i>Red Duchess</i> for her socialist activism), became the highest ranking <a href="/wiki/Spanish_nobility" title="Spanish nobility">Spanish noble</a> to marry in an <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Articulo_mortis" title="Articulo mortis">articulo mortis</a></i> (deathbed) wedding to longtime companion Liliana Maria Dahlmann, now the <a href="/wiki/Dowager" title="Dowager">Dowager Duchess</a> of Medina Sidonia by right of her late wife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rebel_Duchess_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rebel_Duchess-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Red_Duchess_1_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Red_Duchess_1-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dowager_Duchess_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dowager_Duchess-104">[104]</a></sup> In June 2015, the then mayor of the Basque capital <a href="/wiki/Vitoria-Gasteiz" title="Vitoria-Gasteiz">Vitoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Javier_Maroto" title="Javier Maroto">Javier Maroto</a>, announced his engagement to longtime partner Josema Rodríguez. The wedding was held on 18 September 2015 at Vitoria's City Hall. Maroto, a member of the conservative <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">People's Party</a>'s national board, is known for his views contrary to the stance of his own party pertaining to same-sex marriage in Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">Mariano Rajoy</a>, who had challenged the law approving same sex marriage when he was Opposition Leader, attended the wedding celebrations as a guest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_opinion">Public opinion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Same-sex_marriage_in_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Public opinion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A poll by the government-run Centre for Sociological Investigations (<i>Centro de Investigaciones Sociológicas</i>), published in April 2005, reported that 66% of Spaniards favoured legalising same-sex marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlanOut_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-PlanOut-3">[3]</a></sup> Another poll taken by <i>Instituto Opina</i> a day before the bill passed placed support of the same-sex marriage bill at 62.1% and support of adoption by same-sex couples at 49.1%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> An <i>Instituto Opina</i> poll taken nine months after the bill passed said 61% agreed with the Government's decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 July 2007, the BBVA Foundation published their report <i>Social portrait of Spanish people</i>, which reported that 60% of Spain's population support same-sex marriage. This support occurs mainly among the younger population, between 15 and 34 years old (75%), people with higher education (71%), people not attached to any religion (75.5%), and those identified by left and centre-left political views (71.9%). However, only 44% of the population favor the right of adoption by same-sex couples, in contrast to 42% opposition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>A May 2013 Ipsos poll found that 76% of respondents were in favour of same-sex marriage and another 13% supported other forms of recognition for same-sex couples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the Ifop poll, conducted in May 2013, 71% of Spaniards supported allowing same-sex couples to marry and adopt children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 2015 Eurobarometer found that 84% of Spaniards thought that same-sex marriage should be allowed throughout Europe, 10% were against.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
